      <p><b>Geneva</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">jin-<span style="font-size:90%">EE</span>-və</i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-oxford_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxford-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Genève</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʒənɛv]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:LL-Q150_(fra)-Fhala.K-Gen%C3%A8ve.wav" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/LL-Q150_%28fra%29-Fhala.K-Gen%C3%A8ve.wav" class="internal" title="LL-Q150 (fra)-Fhala.K-Genève.wav">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Arpitan_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arpitan language">Arpitan</a>: <i lang="frp">Genèva</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al" title="Help:IPA/Franco-Provençal">[dzəˈnɛva]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frp-greverin-Dzen%C3%A8va.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/Frp-greverin-Dzen%C3%A8va.ogg" class="internal" title="Frp-greverin-Dzenèva.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Genf</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ɡɛnf]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Genf.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/De-Genf.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Genf.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Ginevra</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[dʒiˈneːvra]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">Romansh</a>: <i lang="rm">Genevra</i>) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Switzerland" title="List of cities in Switzerland">second-most populous</a> city in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>) and the most populous city of <a href="/wiki/Romandy" title="Romandy">Romandy</a>, the French-speaking part of Switzerland. Situated where the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a> exits <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a>, it is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva" title="Canton of Geneva">Republic and Canton of Geneva</a>. </p>
      <p>The municipality (<i>ville de Genève</i>) has a population (as of December 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) of 201,818, and the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">canton</a> (essentially the city and its inner-ring suburbs) has 499,480 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-Stat2018_GE_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stat2018_GE-5">[5]</a></sup> In 2014, the compact <i>agglomération du <a href="/wiki/Grand_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Grand Genève">Grand Genève</a></i> had 946,000 inhabitants in 212 communities in both Switzerland and France.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Within Swiss territory, the commuter area named "<i>Métropole lémanique</i>" contains a population of 1.26 million.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> This area is essentially spread east from Geneva towards the Riviera area (<a href="/wiki/Vevey" title="Vevey">Vevey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a>) and north-east towards <a href="/wiki/Yverdon-les-Bains" title="Yverdon-les-Bains">Yverdon-les-Bains</a>, in the neighbouring canton of <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a>. </p>
      <p>Geneva is a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a>, a financial centre, and a worldwide centre for <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a> due to the presence of numerous <a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organizations</a>, including the headquarters of many agencies of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Geneva hosts the highest number of international organizations in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It is also where the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> were signed, which chiefly concern the treatment of wartime non-combatants and <a href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2017, Geneva was ranked as the world's fifteenth most important <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> for competitiveness by the <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a>, fifth in Europe behind London, Zürich, Frankfurt and Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-GFCI_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI-12">[12]</a></sup> In 2019 Geneva was ranked among the ten most liveable cities in the world by <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer</a> together with Zürich and <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The city has been referred to as the world's most compact metropolis<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and the "Peace Capital".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2017, Geneva was ranked as the seventh <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">most expensive city</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-mercer.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercer.com-16">[16]</a></sup> Geneva was ranked third in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power" title="Purchasing power">purchasing power</a> in a global cities ranking by <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-ubs.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ubs.com-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The city was mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> texts, by <a href="/wiki/Commentarii_de_Bello_Gallico" title="Commentarii de Bello Gallico">Caesar</a>, with the spelling <i>Genava</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> probably from the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Celtic" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Celtic">Celtic</a> *<i lang="cel" title="Celtic languages collective text">genawa-</i> from the stem *<i lang="cel" title="Celtic languages collective text">genu-</i> ("bend, knee"), in the sense of a bending river or <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a>, an etymology shared with the Italian port city of <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> (in Italian <i>Genova</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-celtic_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celtic-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The medieval <a href="/wiki/County_of_Geneva" title="County of Geneva">county of Geneva</a> in <a href="/wiki/Middle_Latin" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Latin">Middle Latin</a> was known as <i>pagus major Genevensis</i> or <i>Comitatus Genevensis</i> (also <i>Gebennensis</i>). After 1400 it became the <i><a href="/wiki/Genevois_(province)" title="Genevois (province)">Genevois</a></i> province of <a href="/wiki/Savoy" title="Savoy">Savoy</a> (albeit not extending to the city proper, until the <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">reformation</a> of the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Geneva">Bishop of Geneva</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: 
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Geneva" title="History of Geneva">History of Geneva</a> and 
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Geneva" title="Timeline of Geneva">Timeline of Geneva</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the Catholic ecclesiastical history, see 
       <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Geneva">bishopric of Geneva</a>.
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Escalade-battle-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Escalade-battle-2.jpg/220px-Escalade-battle-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Escalade-battle-2.jpg/330px-Escalade-battle-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Escalade-battle-2.jpg/440px-Escalade-battle-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="702"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Escalade-battle-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/L%27Escalade" title="L'Escalade">L'Escalade</a>, the failed surprise-attack of 12 December 1602 made by troops sent by 
         <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_I,_Duke_of_Savoy" title="Charles Emmanuel I, Duke of Savoy">Charles Emmanuel I, Duke of Savoy</a>, to take Geneva
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva was an <a href="/wiki/Allobroges" title="Allobroges">Allobrogian</a> border town, fortified against the <a href="/wiki/Helvetii" title="Helvetii">Helvetii</a> tribe,<sup id="cite_ref-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva-21">[21]</a></sup> when the Romans took it in 121 BC. It <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianization of the Roman Empire">became Christian</a> under the Late <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="History of the Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, and acquired its first <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Geneva">bishop</a> in the 5th century, having been connected to the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Vienne" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Vienne">Bishopric of Vienne</a> in the 4th. </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Geneva was ruled by a <a href="/wiki/County_of_Geneva" title="County of Geneva">count</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> until the late 14th century, when it was granted a charter giving it a high degree of self-governance. Around this time, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Savoy" title="House of Savoy">House of Savoy</a> came to at least nominally dominate the city. In the 15th century, an <a href="/wiki/Oligarchy" title="Oligarchy">oligarchic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republican</a> government emerged with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Council_of_Geneva" title="Grand Council of Geneva">Grand Council</a>. In the first half of the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> reached the city, causing religious strife, during which Savoy rule was thrown off and Geneva allied itself with the <a href="/wiki/Old_Swiss_Confederacy" title="Old Swiss Confederacy">Swiss Confederacy</a>. In 1541, with Protestantism on the rise, <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformer</a> and proponent of <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>, became the spiritual leader of the city and established the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Geneva">Republic of Geneva</a>. By the 18th century, Geneva had come under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, which cultivated the city as its own. France tended to be at odds with the ordinary townsfolk, which inspired the failed <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Revolution_of_1782" title="Geneva Revolution of 1782">Geneva Revolution of 1782</a>, an attempt to win representation in the government for men of modest means. In 1798, revolutionary France under the <a href="/wiki/French_Directory" title="French Directory">Directory</a> annexed Geneva. At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, on 1<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>June 1814, Geneva was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Confederation">Swiss Confederation</a>. In 1907, the separation of Church and State was adopted. Geneva flourished in the 19th and 20th centuries, becoming the seat of many international organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/220px-Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/330px-Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg/440px-Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1828" data-file-height="1829"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_by_Sentinel-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Geneva seen from Sentinel-2 Satellite
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva is located at 46°12' North, 6°09' East, at the south-western end of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a> flows out. It is surrounded by three mountain chains, each belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Jura_Mountains" title="Jura Mountains">Jura</a>: the Jura main range lies north-westward, the <a href="/wiki/Vuache" title="Vuache">Vuache</a> southward, and the <a href="/wiki/Sal%C3%A8ve" title="Salève">Salève</a> south-eastward. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg/220px-Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg/330px-Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg/440px-Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1856"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%A8ve_vue_du_Sal%C3%A8ve.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Geneva area seen from the Salève in France. The Jura mountains can be seen on the horizon.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The city covers an area of 15.93&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (6.2&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), while the area of the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva" title="Canton of Geneva">canton</a> is 282&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (108.9&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), including the two small <a href="/wiki/Enclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclave">exclaves</a> of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9ligny" title="Céligny">Céligny</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a>. The part of the lake that is attached to Geneva has an area of 38&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (14.7&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and is sometimes referred to as <i>petit lac</i> (small lake). The canton has only a 4.5-kilometre-long (2.8&nbsp;mi) border with the rest of Switzerland. Of 107.5&nbsp;km (66.8&nbsp;mi) of border, 103 are shared with France, the <a href="/wiki/Ain" title="Ain">Département de l'Ain</a> to the north and west and the <a href="/wiki/Haute-Savoie" title="Haute-Savoie">Département de la Haute-Savoie</a> to the south and east. </p>
      <p>Of the land in the city, 0.24&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (0.093&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), or 1.5%, is used for agricultural purposes, while 0.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (0.19&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), or 3.1%, is forested. The rest of the land, 14.63&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (5.65&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), or 91.8%, is built up (buildings or roads), 0.49&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (0.19&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), or 3.1%, is either rivers or lakes and 0.02&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (4.9 acres), or 0.1%, is wasteland.<sup id="cite_ref-BFS_land_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_land-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Of the built up area, industrial buildings made up 3.4%, housing and buildings made up 46.2% and transportation infrastructure 25.8%, while parks, green belts and sports fields made up 15.7%. Of the agricultural land, 0.3% is used for growing crops. Of the water in the municipality, 0.2% is composed of lakes and 2.9% is rivers and streams.<sup id="cite_ref-BFS_land_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_land-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG/220px-Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG/330px-Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG/440px-Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1854"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Confluence_Rh%C3%B4ne_et_Arve.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Confluence of the Rhône and the Arve
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The altitude of Geneva is 373.6 metres (1,225.7&nbsp;ft) and corresponds to the altitude of the largest of the <a href="/wiki/Pierres_du_Niton" title="Pierres du Niton">Pierres du Niton</a>, two large rocks emerging from the lake which date from the <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_glaciation" title="Wisconsin glaciation">last ice age</a>. This rock was chosen by General <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Henri_Dufour" title="Guillaume Henri Dufour">Guillaume Henri Dufour</a> as the reference point for surveying in Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The second main river of Geneva is the <a href="/wiki/Arve" title="Arve">Arve</a>, which flows into the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a> just west of the city centre. <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> can be seen from Geneva and is an hour's drive from the city. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png/220px-Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png/330px-Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png/440px-Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png 2x" data-file-width="893" data-file-height="545"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Average_Temp_and_Precipitation_Geneva.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Average temperature and precipitation 1961–1990
         <sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of Geneva is a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a>, more specifically an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <b>Cfb</b>). Winters are cool, usually with light frosts at night and thawing conditions during the day. Summers are relatively warm. Precipitation is adequate and is relatively well-distributed throughout the year, although autumn is slightly wetter than other seasons. Ice storms near <a href="/wiki/Lac_L%C3%A9man" class="mw-redirect" title="Lac Léman">Lac Léman</a> are normal in the winter: Geneva can be affected by the <a href="/wiki/Bise" title="Bise">Bise</a>, a north-easterly wind. This can lead to severe icing in winter.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In summer, many people swim in the lake and patronise public beaches such as Genève Plage and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bains_des_P%C3%A2quis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bains des Pâquis (page does not exist)">Bains des Pâquis</a>. The city, in certain years, receives snow during colder months. The nearby mountains are subject to substantial snowfall and are suitable for skiing. Many world-renowned ski resorts such as <a href="/wiki/Verbier" title="Verbier">Verbier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crans-Montana" title="Crans-Montana">Crans-Montana</a> are less than three hours away by car. <a href="/wiki/Saleve" class="mw-redirect" title="Saleve">Mont Salève</a> (1,379&nbsp;m (4,524&nbsp;ft)), just across the border in France, dominates the southerly view from the city centre, and <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a>, the highest of the Alpine range, is visible from most of the city, towering high above <a href="/wiki/Chamonix" title="Chamonix">Chamonix</a>, which, along with Morzine, Le Grand Bornand, La Clusaz, and resorts of the Grand Massif such as Samoens, Morillon, and Flaine, are the closest French skiing destinations to Geneva. </p>
      <p>During the years 2000–2009, the mean yearly temperature was 11&nbsp;°C and the mean number of sunshine-hours per year was 2003.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The highest temperature recorded in Genève–Cointrin was 39.7&nbsp;°C (103.5&nbsp;°F) in July 2015, and the lowest temperature recorded was −20.0&nbsp;°C (−4.0&nbsp;°F) in February 1956. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Geneva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Coat of arms of Geneva as part of the pavement in front of the 
         <a href="/wiki/Reformation_Wall" title="Reformation Wall">Reformation Wall</a>, 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The city is divided into eight <i>quartiers</i>, or districts, sometimes composed of several neighbourhoods. On the left bank are: (1) Jonction, (2) Centre, <a href="/wiki/Plainpalais" title="Plainpalais">Plainpalais</a>, and Acacias; (3) Eaux-Vives; and (4) <a href="/wiki/Champel" title="Champel">Champel</a>. The right bank includes: (1) Saint-Jean and Charmilles; (2) <a href="/wiki/Servette" title="Servette">Servette</a> and Petit-Saconnex; (3) Grottes and Saint-Gervais; and (4) Paquis and Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Geneva" title="List of mayors of Geneva">List of mayors of Geneva</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_city_insignia.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geneva_city_insignia.gif/220px-Geneva_city_insignia.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geneva_city_insignia.gif/330px-Geneva_city_insignia.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Geneva_city_insignia.gif/440px-Geneva_city_insignia.gif 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="279"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_city_insignia.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Logo of the city of Geneva, 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Administrative Council (<b>Conseil administratif</b>) constitutes the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> government of the City of Geneva and operates as a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Collegiate_authority&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Collegiate authority (page does not exist)">collegiate authority</a>. It is composed of five councilors (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Conseiller administratif/ Conseillère administrative</i>), each presiding over a department. The president of the executive department acts as <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> (<i>la maire/le maire</i>). In the governmental year 2019–2020, the Administrative Council is presided over by <i>Madame la maire de Genève</i> <a href="/wiki/Sandrine_Salerno" title="Sandrine Salerno">Sandrine Salerno</a>. Departmental tasks, coordination measures and implementation of laws decreed by the Municipal Council are carried out by the Administrative Council. Elections for the Administrative Council are held every five years. The current term of (<i>la législature</i>) is from 1<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>June 2015 to 31<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>May 2020. The delegates are elected by means of a system of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Majorz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Majorz (page does not exist)">Majorz</a>. The mayor changes each year, while the heads of the other departments are assigned by the collegiate. The executive body holds its meetings in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palais_Eynard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palais Eynard (page does not exist)">Palais Eynard</a>, near the Parc des Bastions.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Geneva's Administrative Council is made up of two representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">Social Democratic Party</a> (PS), and one member each of: the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Party of Switzerland">Green Party</a> (PES); <i>Ensemble à Gauche</i> (an alliance of left-wing parties); the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Party_of_Labour" title="Swiss Party of Labour">Swiss Party of Labour</a>; <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Switzerland)" title="Solidarity (Switzerland)">solidaritéS</a>); and the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">Christian Democratic Party</a> (PDC). This gives the left-wing parties four out of the five seats. The last election was held on 19<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>April 2015. All previous members were re-elected.<sup id="cite_ref-CA_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CA-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_Council">Municipal Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Municipal Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style="">

         </div> 
        </div>

      <p>The Municipal Council (<b>Conseil municipal</b>) holds <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a>. It is made up of 80 members, with elections held every five years. The Municipal Council makes regulations and by-laws that are executed by the Administrative Council and the administration. The delegates are selected by means of a system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> with a seven percent threshold. </p>
      <p>The sessions of the Municipal Council are public. Unlike members of the Administrative Council, members of the Municipal Council are not politicians by profession, and they are paid a fee based on their attendance. Any resident of Geneva allowed to vote can be elected as a member of the Municipal Council. The Council holds its meetings in the Town Hall (<i>Hôtel de Ville</i>), in the old city.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The last election of the Municipal Council was held on 20<span class="nowrap">&nbsp;</span>April 2015 for the (<i>législature</i>) of 2015–2020. Currently, the Municipal Council consist of: 19 members of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">Social Democratic Party (PS)</a>; 15 <a href="/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals" title="FDP.The Liberals">Les Libéraux-Radicaux (PLR)</a>; 11 <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">Christian Democratic People's Party (PDC)</a>; 11 <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Citizens%27_Movement" title="Geneva Citizens' Movement">Geneva Citizens' Movement (MCG,)</a>; 10 <i>Ensemble à Gauche</i> (an alliance of the left parties <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Party_of_Labour" title="Swiss Party of Labour">PST-POP</a> (<i>Parti Suisse du Travail – Parti Ouvrier et Populaire</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Switzerland)" title="Solidarity (Switzerland)">solidaritéS</a>); 8 <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Party of Switzerland">Green Party (PES)</a>; and 6 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">Swiss People's Party (UDC)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Council">National Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: National Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_federal_election,_2015" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss federal election, 2015">2015 federal election</a> for the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_(Switzerland)" title="National Council (Switzerland)">Swiss National Council</a> the most popular party was the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">PS</a> which received 23.8% of the vote. The next five most popular parties were the <a href="/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals" title="FDP.The Liberals">PLR</a> (17.6%), the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">UDC</a> (16.3%), the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Party of Switzerland">Green Party</a> (11.4%), the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">PDC</a> (10.7%), and the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Switzerland)" title="Solidarity (Switzerland)">solidaritéS</a> (8.8%). In the federal election a total of 36,490 votes were cast, and the <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a> was 44.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Geneva intentionally does not have any <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">sister</a> relationships with other cities. It declares itself related to the entire world.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         <a href="/wiki/L%27horloge_fleurie" title="L'horloge fleurie">The Flowered Clock</a> at the Quai du Général-Guisan (
         <a href="/wiki/Jardin_Anglais" title="Jardin Anglais">English Garden</a>), during the 2012 
         <a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Fêtes de Genève">Geneva Festival</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rue_Pierre-Fatio,_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg/220px-Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg/330px-Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg/440px-Rue_Pierre-Fatio%2C_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rue_Pierre-Fatio,_Gen%C3%A8ve.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Rue Pierre-Fatio in Geneva
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva has a population (as of December 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) of 201,818.<sup id="cite_ref-Stat2018_GE_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stat2018_GE-5">[5]</a></sup> The city of Geneva is at the centre of the Geneva metropolitan area, known as <i>Grand Genève</i> in French (Greater Geneva). Greater Geneva includes the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva" title="Canton of Geneva">Canton of Geneva</a> in its entirety as well as the <a href="/wiki/Nyon_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyon (district)">District of Nyon</a> in the Canton of <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a> and several areas in the neighbouring French <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Haute-Savoie" title="Haute-Savoie">Haute-Savoie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ain" title="Ain">Ain</a>. In 2011, the <i>agglomération franco-valdo-genevoise</i> had 915,000 inhabitants, two-thirds of whom lived on Swiss soil and one-third on French soil.<sup id="cite_ref-metro_area_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro_area-41">[39]</a></sup> The Geneva metropolitan area is experiencing steady demographic growth of 1.2% a year and the population of the <i>agglomération franco-valdo-genevoise</i> is expected to reach a total of one million people in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-metro_area_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro_area-41">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official language of Geneva (both the city and the canton) is <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. English is also common due to the high number of anglophone expatriates and foreigners working in international institutions and in the bank sector. As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 128,622 or 72.3% of the population speaks French as a first language, with English being the second most common (7,853 or 4.4%) language. 7,462 inhabitants speak Spanish (or 4.2%), 7,320 speak Italian (4.1%), 7,050 speak German (4.0%) and 113 people who speak <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">Romansh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-STAT2000_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-42">[40]</a></sup> As a result of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Switzerland" title="Immigration to Switzerland">immigration</a> flows in the 1960s and 1980s, Italian, Portuguese and Spanish are also spoken by a considerable proportion of the population. </p>
      <p>In the city of Geneva, as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 48% of the population are resident foreign nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> For a list of the largest groups of foreign residents <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva#Demographics" title="Canton of Geneva">see the cantonal overview</a>. Over the last 10 years (1999–2009), the population has changed at a rate of 7.2%; a rate of 3.4% due to migration and at a rate of 3.4% due to births and deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the gender distribution of the population was 47.8% male and 52.2% female. The male population was made up of 46,284 Swiss men (24.2% of the population) and 45,127 (23.6%) non-Swiss men. There were 56,091 Swiss women (29.3%) and 43,735 (22.9%) non-Swiss women.<sup id="cite_ref-GE_Pop_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GE_Pop-45">[43]</a></sup> As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> approximately 24.3% of the population of the municipality were born in Geneva and lived there in 2000&nbsp;– 43,296. A further 11,757 or 6.6% who were born in the same canton, while 27,359 or 15.4% were born elsewhere in Switzerland, and 77,893 or 43.8% were born outside of Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-STAT2000_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 1,147 live births to Swiss citizens and 893 births to non-Swiss citizens, and in the same time span there were 1,114 deaths of Swiss citizens and 274 non-Swiss citizen deaths. Ignoring immigration and emigration, the population of Swiss citizens increased by 33, while the foreign population increased by 619. There were 465 Swiss men and 498 Swiss women who emigrated from Switzerland. At the same time, there were 2933 non-Swiss men and 2662 non-Swiss women who immigrated from another country to Switzerland. The total Swiss population change in 2008 (from all sources, including moves across municipal borders) was an increase of 135 and the non-Swiss population increased by 3181 people. This represents a <a href="/wiki/Population_growth#Population_growth_rate" title="Population growth">population growth rate</a> of 1.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-HDS_superweb_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDS_superweb-46">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, children and teenagers (0–19 years old) make up 18.2% of the population, while adults (20–64 years old) make up 65.8% and seniors (over 64 years old) make up 16%.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 78,666 people who were single and never married in the municipality. There were 74,205 married individuals, 10,006 widows or widowers and 15,087 individuals who are divorced.<sup id="cite_ref-STAT2000_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 86,231 private households in the municipality, and an average of 1.9 persons per household.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> There were 44,373 households that consist of only one person and 2,549 households with five or more people. Out of a total of 89,269 households that answered this question, 49.7% were households made up of just one person and there were 471 adults who lived with their parents. Of the rest of the households, there are 17,429 married couples without children, 16,607 married couples with children. There were 5,499 single parents with a child or children. There were 1,852 households that were made up of unrelated people and 3,038 households that were made up of some sort of institution or another collective housing.<sup id="cite_ref-STAT2000_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-42">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg/220px-Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg/330px-Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg/440px-Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3652" data-file-height="2445"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva_-_Quartier_des_Grottes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Apartment buildings in the Quartier des Grottes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva-aerial-view.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Geneva-aerial-view.JPG/220px-Geneva-aerial-view.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Geneva-aerial-view.JPG/330px-Geneva-aerial-view.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Geneva-aerial-view.JPG/440px-Geneva-aerial-view.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2720" data-file-height="2040"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geneva-aerial-view.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Geneva, with Lake Geneva in the background
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 743 single family homes (or 10.6% of the total) out of a total of 6,990 inhabited buildings. There were 2,758 multi-family buildings (39.5%), along with 2,886 multi-purpose buildings that were mostly used for housing (41.3%) and 603 other use buildings (commercial or industrial) that also had some housing (8.6%). Of the single family homes, 197 were built before 1919, while 20 were built between 1990 and 2000. The greatest number of single family homes (277) were built between 1919 and 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Housing_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Housing-47">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 101,794 apartments in the municipality. The most common apartment size was 3 rooms of which there were 27,084. There were 21,889 single room apartments and 11,166 apartments with five or more rooms. Of these apartments, a total of 85,330 apartments (83.8% of the total) were permanently occupied, while 13,644 apartments (13.4%) were seasonally occupied and 2,820 apartments (2.8%) were empty.<sup id="cite_ref-Housing_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Housing-47">[45]</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the construction rate of new housing units was 1.3 new units per 1000 residents.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2003<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the average price to rent an average apartment in Geneva was 1163.30 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss francs</a> (CHF) per month (US$930, £520, €740 approx. exchange rate from 2003). The average rate for a one-room apartment was 641.60 CHF (US$510, £290, €410), a two-room apartment was about 874.46 CHF (US$700, £390, €560), a three-room apartment was about 1126.37 CHF (US$900, £510, €720) and a six or more room apartment cost an average of 2691.07 CHF (US$2150, £1210, €1720). The average apartment price in Geneva was 104.2% of the national average of 1116 CHF.<sup id="cite_ref-BFS_rent_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_rent-48">[46]</a></sup> The vacancy rate for the municipality, in 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, was 0.25%.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2011, the average price of an apartment in and around Geneva was 13,681 CHF per square metre (11 square feet). The average can be as high as 17,589 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss francs</a> (CHF) per square metre (11 square feet) for a luxury apartment and as low as 9,847 Swiss francs (CHF) for an older or basic apartment. For houses in and around Geneva, the average price was 11,595 Swiss francs (CHF) per square metre (11 square feet) (June 2011), with a lowest price per square metre (11 square feet) of 4,874 Swiss francs (CHF), and a maximum price of 21,966 Swiss francs (CHF).<sup id="cite_ref-homech_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homech-49">[47]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_population">Historical population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Historical population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>William Monter calculates that the city's total population was 12,000–13,000 in 1550, doubling to over 25,000 by 1560.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 2000 census<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> recorded 66,491 residents (37.4% of the population) as Roman Catholic, while 41,289 people (23.20%) belonged to no church or were <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a>, 24,105 (13.5%) belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church" title="Swiss Reformed Church">Swiss Reformed Church</a>, and 8,698 (4.89%) were <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>. There were also 3,959 members of an <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox church</a> (2.22%), 220 individuals (or about 0.12% of the population) who belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Catholic_Church_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Catholic Church of Switzerland">Christian Catholic Church of Switzerland</a>, 2,422 (1.36%) who belonged to another Christian church, and 2,601 people (1.46%) who were <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a>. There were 707 individuals who were Buddhist, 474 who were Hindu and 423 who belonged to another church. 26,575 respondents (14.93%) did not answer the question.<sup id="cite_ref-STAT2000_42-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-42">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to 2012 statistics by Swiss Bundesamt für Statistik 49.2% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>, divided into 34.2% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, 8.8% <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Reformed">Swiss Reformed</a> (organized in the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Church_of_Geneva" title="Protestant Church of Geneva">Protestant Church of Geneva</a>) and 6.2% other Christian (mostly various other <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>), 38% of Genevans are <a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">non-religious</a>, 6.1% are <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> and 1.6% are <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Geneva has historically been considered a <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> city and was known as the <i>Protestant Rome</i> due to it being the base of <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">William Farel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Beza" title="Theodore Beza">Theodore Beza</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Protestant_reformers" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant reformers">Protestant reformers</a>. Over the past century, substantial immigration from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and other predominantly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> countries, as well as general <a href="/wiki/Post-Christian_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-Christian Europe">European secularization</a> has changed its religious landscape. As a result, three times as many Roman Catholics as Protestants lived in the city in 2000, while a large number of residents were members of neither group. Geneva forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Lausanne,_Geneva_and_Fribourg" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Lausanne, Geneva and Fribourg">Roman Catholic Diocese of Lausanne, Geneva and Fribourg</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Council_of_Churches" title="World Council of Churches">World Council of Churches</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_World_Federation" title="Lutheran World Federation">Lutheran World Federation</a> both have their headquarters at the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Centre" title="Ecumenical Centre">Ecumenical Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Grand-Saconnex" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand-Saconnex">Grand-Saconnex</a>, Geneva. The <a href="/wiki/World_Communion_of_Reformed_Churches" title="World Communion of Reformed Churches">World Communion of Reformed Churches</a>, a worldwide organization of <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Reformed">Continental Reformed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Congregational" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregational">Congregational</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Reformed" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> churches gathering more than 80 million people around the world was based here from 1948 until 2013. The Executive Committee of the <a href="/wiki/World_Communion_of_Reformed_Churches" title="World Communion of Reformed Churches">World Communion of Reformed Churches</a> voted in 2012 to move its offices to <a href="/wiki/Hanover,_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanover, Germany">Hanover, Germany</a>, citing the high costs of running the ecumenical organization in Geneva, Switzerland. The move was completed in 2013. Likewise, the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_European_Churches" title="Conference of European Churches">Conference of European Churches</a> have moved their headquarters from Geneva to Brussels. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_Rome">Protestant Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Protestant Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg/220px-ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg/330px-ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg/440px-ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ReformationsdenkmalGenf1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Reformation_Wall" title="Reformation Wall">Reformation Wall</a> in Geneva; from left to right: 
         <a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">William Farel</a>, 
         <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a>, 
         <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Beza" title="Theodore Beza">Theodore Beza</a>, and 
         <a href="/wiki/John_Knox" title="John Knox">John Knox</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> the city was <i>de jure</i> and <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>. Reaction to the new movement varied across Switzerland. <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a> went to Geneva in 1536 after <a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">William Farel</a> encouraged him to do so. In Geneva, the Catholic bishop had been obliged to seek exile in 1532. Geneva became a stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>. Some of the tenets created there influenced Protestantism as a whole. <a href="/wiki/St._Pierre_Cathedral" title="St. Pierre Cathedral">St. Pierre Cathedral</a> was where Calvin and his <a href="/wiki/Protestant_reformers" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant reformers">Protestant reformers</a> preached. It constituted the epicentre of the newly developing Protestant thought that would later become known as the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed tradition</a>. Many prominent Reformed theologians operated there, including <a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">William Farel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Beza" title="Theodore Beza">Theodore Beza</a>, Calvin's successor who progressed Reformed thought after his death. </p>
      <p>Geneva was a shelter for Calvinists, but at the same time it persecuted Roman Catholics and others considered heretics. The case of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Servetus" title="Michael Servetus">Michael Servetus</a>, an early <a href="/wiki/Nontrinitarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Nontrinitarian">Nontrinitarian</a>, is notable. Condemned by Catholics and Protestants alike, he was arrested in Geneva and burnt at the stake as a heretic by order of the city's Protestant governing council. John Calvin and his followers denounced him, and possibly contributed to his sentence. </p>
      <p>In 1802, during its annexation to France under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon I</a>, the Diocese of Geneva was united with the Diocese of Chambéry, but the 1814 Congress of Vienna and the 1816 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turin_(1816)" title="Treaty of Turin (1816)">Treaty of Turin</a> stipulated that in the territories transferred to a now considerably extended Geneva, the Catholic religion was to be protected and that no changes were to be made in existing conditions without an agreement with the Holy See.<sup id="cite_ref-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva-21">[21]</a></sup> Napoleon's common policy was to emancipate Catholics in Protestant-majority areas, and the other way around, as well as emancipating Jews. In 1819, the city of Geneva and 20 parishes were united to the Diocese of Lausanne by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_VII" title="Pope Pius VII">Pope Pius VII</a> and in 1822, the non-Swiss territory was made into the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Annecy" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Annecy">Diocese of Annecy</a>. A variety of concord with the civil authorities came as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a>, enacted with strong Catholic support in 1907.<sup id="cite_ref-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CathEncy-LausanneGeneva-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Switzerland" title="Crime in Switzerland">Crime in Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2014 the incidence of crimes listed in the <a href="/wiki/Strafgesetzbuch_(Switzerland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strafgesetzbuch (Switzerland)">Swiss Criminal Code</a> in Geneva was 143.9 per thousand residents. During the same period the rate of drug crimes was 33.6 per thousand residents. The rate of violations of immigration, visa and work permit laws was 35.7 per thousand residents.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Heritage_sites_of_national_significance">Heritage sites of national significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Heritage sites of national significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>There are 82 buildings or sites in Geneva that are listed as Swiss <a href="/wiki/Swiss_inventory_of_cultural_property_of_national_and_regional_significance" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss inventory of cultural property of national and regional significance">heritage sites of national significance</a>, and the entire old city of Geneva is part of the <a href="/wiki/Inventory_of_Swiss_Heritage_Sites" title="Inventory of Swiss Heritage Sites">Inventory of Swiss Heritage Sites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>Religious buildings:</b> <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">Cathedral</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Pierre_Cathedral" title="St. Pierre Cathedral">St-Pierre</a> et Chapel des Macchabés, Notre-Dame Church, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Church,_Geneva" title="Russian Church, Geneva">Russian church</a>, St-Germain Church, Temple de la Fusterie, Temple de l'Auditoire </p>
      <p><b>Civic buildings:</b> Former Arsenal and Archives of the City of Genève, Former Crédit Lyonnais, Former Hôtel Buisson, Former Hôtel du Résident de France et Bibliothèque de la Société de lecture de Genève, Former école des arts industriels, Archives d'État de Genève (Annexe), Bâtiment des forces motrices, <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Bibliothèque de Genève">Bibliothèque de Genève</a>, Library juive de Genève «Gérard Nordmann», Cabinet des estampes, Centre d'Iconographie genevoise, <a href="/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_Calvin" title="Collège Calvin">Collège Calvin</a>, École Geisendorf, <a href="/wiki/University_Hospital_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="University Hospital of Geneva">University Hospital of Geneva</a> (HUG), Hôtel de Ville et tour Baudet, <a href="/wiki/Immeuble_Clart%C3%A9" title="Immeuble Clarté">Immeuble Clarté</a> at Rue Saint-Laurent 2 and 4, Immeubles House Rotonde at Rue Charles-Giron 11–19, Immeubles at Rue Beauregard 2, 4, 6, 8, Immeubles at Rue de la Corraterie 10–26, Immeubles at Rue des Granges 2–6, Immeuble at Rue des Granges 8, Immeubles at Rue des Granges 10 and 12, Immeuble at Rue des Granges 14, Immeuble and Former Armory at Rue des Granges 16, Immeubles at Rue Pierre Fatio 7 and 9, House de Saussure at Rue de la Cité 24, House Des arts du Grütli at Rue du Général-Dufour 16, House Royale et les deux immeubles à côté at Quai Gustave Ador 44–50, Tavel House at Rue du Puits-St-Pierre 6, Turrettini House at Rue de l'Hôtel-de-Ville 8 and 10, Brunswick Monument, Palais de Justice, Palais de l'Athénée, Palais des Nations with library and archives of the SDN and ONU, Palais Eynard et Archives de la ville de Genève, <a href="/wiki/Palais_Wilson" title="Palais Wilson">Palais Wilson</a>, Parc des Bastions avec Mur des Réformateurs, Place de Neuve et Monument du Général Dufour, Pont de la Machine, Pont sur l'Arve, Poste du Mont-Blanc, Quai du Mont-Blanc, Quai et Hôtel des Bergues, Quai Général Guisan and English Gardens, Quai Gustave-Ador and Jet d'eau, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision_Suisse_Romande" title="Télévision Suisse Romande">Télévision Suisse Romande</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Geneva" title="University of Geneva">University of Geneva</a>, Victoria Hall. </p>
      <p><b>Archeological sites:</b> Foundation Baur and Museum of the arts d'Extrême-Orient, Parc et campagne de la Grange and Library (neolithic shore settlement/Roman villa), <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> shore settlement of Plonjon, Temple de la Madeleine archeological site, Temple Saint-Gervais archeological site, Old City with <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_in_the_Roman_era" title="Switzerland in the Roman era">Roman</a> and medieval villages. </p>
      <p><b>Museums, theaters, and other cultural sites:</b> Conservatoire de musique at Place Neuve 5, Conservatoire et Jardin botaniques, Fonds cantonal d'art contemporain, Ile Rousseau and statue, <a href="/wiki/Institut_et_Mus%C3%A9e_Voltaire" title="Institut et Musée Voltaire">Institut et Musée Voltaire</a> with Library and Archives, Mallet House and Museum international de la Réforme, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Ariana" title="Musée Ariana">Musée Ariana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_d%27Art_et_d%27Histoire_(Geneva)" title="Musée d'Art et d'Histoire (Geneva)">Museum of Art and History</a>, Museum d'art moderne et contemporain, Museum d'ethnographie, <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Museum" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Museum">Museum of the International Red Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Rath" title="Musée Rath">Musée Rath</a>, Natural History Museum, Plainpalais Commune Auditorium, Pitoëff Theatre, Villa Bartholoni at the Museum of History and Science. </p>
      <p><b>International organizations:</b> <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (BIT), <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (UNHCR), <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>, World Alliance of <a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">Young Men's Christian Association</a> </p>
