      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The city's main newspaper is the daily <i><a href="/wiki/Tribune_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Tribune de Genève">Tribune de Genève</a></i>, with a readership of about 187,000. <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Courrier" title="Le Courrier">Le Courrier</a></i> mainly focuses on Geneva. Both <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Temps" title="Le Temps">Le Temps</a></i> (headquartered in Geneva) and <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Matin_(Switzerland)" title="Le Matin (Switzerland)">Le Matin</a></i> are widely read in Geneva, but cover the whole of <a href="/wiki/Romandy" title="Romandy">Romandy</a>. </p>
      <p>Geneva is the main media center for French-speaking Switzerland. It is the headquarters for the numerous <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_network" title="Radio network">radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television_network" title="Television network">television</a> networks of the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Swiss Broadcasting Corporation">Swiss Broadcasting Corporation</a>, known collectively as <a href="/wiki/Radio_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision_Suisse" title="Radio Télévision Suisse">Radio Télévision Suisse</a>. While both networks cover the whole of <a href="/wiki/Romandy" title="Romandy">Romandy</a>, special programs related to Geneva are sometimes broadcast on some of the local radio frequencies. Other local radio stations broadcast from the city, including YesFM (<a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> 91.8&nbsp;MHz), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Radio_Cit%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Radio Cité (page does not exist)">Radio Cité</a> (non-commercial radio, FM 92.2&nbsp;MHz), OneFM (FM 107.0&nbsp;MHz, also broadcast in <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a>), and <a href="/wiki/World_Radio_Switzerland" title="World Radio Switzerland">World Radio Switzerland</a> (FM 88.4&nbsp;MHz). Léman Bleu is a local TV channel, founded in 1996 and distributed by cable. Due to the proximity to France, many <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_stations_in_France" title="List of television stations in France">French television channels</a> are also available. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions_and_customs">Traditions and customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Traditions and customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Geneva observes <i><a href="/wiki/Je%C3%BBne_genevois" title="Jeûne genevois">Jeûne genevois</a></i> on the first Thursday following the first Sunday in September. By local tradition, this commemorates the date news of the <a href="/wiki/St._Bartholomew%27s_Day_massacre" title="St. Bartholomew's Day massacre">St. Bartholomew's Day massacre</a> of Huguenots reached Geneva. </p>
      <p>Geneva celebrates <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Escalade" title="L'Escalade">L'Escalade</a></i> on the weekend nearest 12 December, celebrating the defeat of the surprise attack of troops sent by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Emmanuel_I,_Duke_of_Savoy" title="Charles Emmanuel I, Duke of Savoy">Charles Emmanuel I, Duke of Savoy</a> during the night of 11–12 December 1602. Festive traditions include chocolate cauldrons filled with vegetable-shaped marzipan treats and the Escalade procession on horseback in seventeenth century armour. Geneva has also been organizing a 'Course de l'Escalade', which means 'Climbing Race'. This race takes place in Geneva's Old Town, and has been popular across all ages. Non-competitive racers dress up in fancy costumes, while walking in the race. </p>
      <p>Since 1818, a particular <a href="/wiki/Chestnut" title="Chestnut">chestnut tree</a> has been used as the official "herald of the spring" in Geneva. The <i>sautier</i> (secretary of the Parliament of the Canton of Geneva) observes the tree and notes the day of arrival of the first bud. While this event has no practical effect, the sautier issues a formal <a href="/wiki/News_release" class="mw-redirect" title="News release">press release</a> and the local newspaper will usually mention the news.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As this is one of the world's oldest records of a plant's reaction to climatic conditions, researchers have been interested to note that the first bud has been appearing earlier and earlier in the year. During the 19th century many dates were in March or April. In recent years, they have usually been in late February (sometimes earlier).<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> In 2002, the first bud appeared unusually early, on 7 February, and then again on 29 December of the same year. The following year, one of the hottest years recorded in Europe, was a year with no bud. In 2008, the first bud also appeared early, on 19 February. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_festivals">Music and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_(54).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg/220px-Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg/330px-Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg/440px-Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_%2854%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fireworks_at_the_F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve_2012_-_panoramio_(54).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fireworks at the Fêtes de Genève, 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera house</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Th%C3%A9%C3%A2tre_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Grand Théâtre de Genève">Grand Théâtre de Genève</a>, which officially opened in 1876, was partly destroyed by a fire in 1951 and reopened in 1962. It has the largest stage in Switzerland. It features opera and dance performances, recitals, concerts and, occasionally, theatre. The <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Hall_(Geneva)" title="Victoria Hall (Geneva)">Victoria Hall</a> is used for classical music concerts. It is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Orchestre_de_la_Suisse_Romande" title="Orchestre de la Suisse Romande">Orchestre de la Suisse Romande</a>. </p>
      <p>Every summer the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAtes_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Fêtes de Genève">Fêtes de Genève</a> (Geneva Festival) are organised in Geneva. According to <a href="/wiki/Radio_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision_Suisse" title="Radio Télévision Suisse">Radio Télévision Suisse</a> in 2013 hundreds of thousands of people came to Geneva to see the annual hour-long grand <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">firework</a> display of the Fêtes de Genève.<sup id="cite_ref-rts.ch_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rts.ch-57">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An annual music festival takes place in June. Groups of artists perform in different parts of the city. In 2016 the festival celebrated its 25th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-Official_website_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_website-58">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg/220px-Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg/330px-Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg/440px-Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maison_de_la_paix_petals_1_and_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Institute_of_International_and_Development_Studies" title="Graduate Institute of International and Development Studies">Graduate Institute of International and Development Studies</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Canton of Geneva's <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">public school</a> system has <i>écoles primaires</i> (ages 4–12) and <i>cycles d'orientation</i> (ages 12–15). Students can leave school at 15, but secondary education is provided by <i>collèges</i> (ages 15–19), the oldest of which is the <a href="/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_Calvin" title="Collège Calvin">Collège Calvin</a>, which could be considered one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">public schools</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-rts.ch_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rts.ch-57">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> <i>écoles de culture générale</i> (15-18/19) and the <i>écoles professionnelles</i> (15-18/19). The <i>écoles professionnelles</i> offer full-time courses and part-time study as part of an apprenticeship. Geneva also has a number of private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011 89,244 (37.0%) of the population had completed non-mandatory upper secondary education, and 107,060 or (44.3%) had completed additional higher education (either university or a Fachhochschule). Of the 107,060 who completed tertiary schooling, 32.5% were Swiss men, 31.6% were Swiss women, 18.1% were non-Swiss men and 17.8% were non-Swiss women. </p>
      <p>During the 2011–2012 school year, there were a total of 92,311 students in the Geneva school system (primary to university). The education system in the Canton of Geneva has eight years of primary school, with 32,716 students. The secondary school program consists of three lower, obligatory years of schooling, followed by three to five years of optional, advanced study. There were 13,146 lower-secondary students who attended schools in Geneva. There were 10,486 upper-secondary students from the municipality along with 10,330 students who were in a professional, non-university track program. An additional 11,797 students were attending private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:University_Geneva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/University_Geneva.jpg/220px-University_Geneva.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/University_Geneva.jpg/330px-University_Geneva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/University_Geneva.jpg/440px-University_Geneva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:University_Geneva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Geneva" title="University of Geneva">University of Geneva</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Geneva" title="University of Geneva">University of Geneva</a>. In 1559 <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a> founded the Geneva Academy, a theological and humanist seminary. In the 19th century the Academy lost its ecclesiastic links and in 1873, with the addition of a medical faculty, it became the University of Geneva. In 2011 it was ranked 35th European university.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Institute_of_International_and_Development_Studies" title="Graduate Institute of International and Development Studies">Graduate Institute of International and Development Studies</a> was among the first academic institutions in the World to teach international relations. It is one of Europe's most prestigious institutions, offering MA and PhD programmes in law, political science, history, economics, international affairs, and development studies. </p>
      <p>The oldest <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international school</a> in the world is the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Geneva" title="International School of Geneva">International School of Geneva</a>, founded in 1924 along with the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Geneva_School_of_Diplomacy_and_International_Relations" title="Geneva School of Diplomacy and International Relations">Geneva School of Diplomacy and International Relations</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private university</a> in the grounds of the Château de Penthes. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> (the European Organization for Nuclear Research) is probably the best known of Geneva's educational and research facilities, most recently for the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a>. Founded in 1954, CERN was one of Europe's first <a href="/wiki/Joint_venture" title="Joint venture">joint ventures</a> and has developed as the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a> <a href="/wiki/Laboratory" title="Laboratory">laboratory</a>. Physicists from around the world travel to CERN to research matter and explore the fundamental forces and materials that form the universe. </p>
      <p>Geneva is home to five major libraries, the <i>Bibliothèques municipales Genève</i>, the <i>Haute école de travail social, Institut d'études sociales</i>, the <i>Haute école de santé</i>, the <i>Ecole d'ingénieurs de Genève</i> and the <i>Haute école d'art et de design</i>. There were (as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) 877,680 books or other media in the libraries, and in the same year 1,798,980 items were loaned.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG/220px-IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG/330px-IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG/440px-IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:IntAutoSalonGenf08.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">Geneva Motor Show</a>, 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva's economy is <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">services</a> oriented. The city has an important and long-established <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">finance sector</a>, which specialises in <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">private banking</a>, managing assets of about US$1 trillion, and the financing of international trade. In the September 2017 <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centres Index</a>, Geneva was ranked as being the 15th most competitive financial centre in the world (up from 20th in March 2017) and the fifth most competitive in Europe (after <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_London#Financial_services" title="Economy of London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich#Economy" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Luxembourg#Banking" title="Economy of Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-GFCI_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Geneva hosts the international headquarters of companies such as <a href="/wiki/Japan_Tobacco_International" title="Japan Tobacco International">Japan Tobacco International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Shipping_Company_S.A." class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean Shipping Company S.A.">Mediterranean Shipping Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitol" title="Vitol">Vitol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gunvor_(company)" title="Gunvor (company)">Gunvor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercuria_Energy_Group" title="Mercuria Energy Group">Mercuria Energy Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merck_Serono" title="Merck Serono">Merck Serono</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SITA_(IT_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="SITA (IT company)">SITA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_de_Surveillance" class="mw-redirect" title="Société Générale de Surveillance">Société Générale de Surveillance</a>, <a href="/wiki/STMicroelectronics" title="STMicroelectronics">STMicroelectronics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weatherford_International" title="Weatherford International">Weatherford International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Many other <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational companies</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar</a>, <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">DuPont</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cargill" title="Cargill">Cargill</a> have their international headquarters in the city; <a href="/wiki/Take-Two_Interactive" title="Take-Two Interactive">Take Two Interactive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/INVISTA" class="mw-redirect" title="INVISTA">INVISTA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a> have their European headquarters in the city. <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard" class="mw-redirect" title="Hewlett Packard">Hewlett Packard</a> has its Europe, Africa, and Middle East headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Meyrin" title="Meyrin">Meyrin</a>, near Geneva,<sup id="cite_ref-Meyrinmap_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyrinmap-66">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> as does <a href="/wiki/PrivatAir" title="PrivatAir">PrivatAir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There is a long tradition of <a href="/wiki/Watchmaker" title="Watchmaker">watchmaking</a> in the city, which dates back to the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> Many watchmakers have been based in Geneva since their foundation, such as (<a href="/wiki/Baume_et_Mercier" title="Baume et Mercier">Baume et Mercier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charriol" title="Charriol">Charriol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chopard" title="Chopard">Chopard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franck_Muller" title="Franck Muller">Franck Muller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patek_Philippe_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Patek Philippe &amp; Co.">Patek Philippe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rolex" title="Rolex">Rolex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Universal Genève">Universal Genève</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Weil" title="Raymond Weil">Raymond Weil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vacheron_Constantin" title="Vacheron Constantin">Vacheron Constantin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9rique_Constant" title="Frédérique Constant">Frédérique Constant</a>). </p>
      <p>Two major international producers of flavours and fragrances, <a href="/wiki/Firmenich" title="Firmenich">Firmenich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Givaudan" title="Givaudan">Givaudan</a>, have their headquarters and main production facilities in Geneva. </p>
      <p>The private sector has a number of <a href="/wiki/Employers%27_organization" title="Employers' organization">employers' organizations</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_des_Entreprises_Romandes_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Fédération des Entreprises Romandes Genève">Fédération des Entreprises Romandes Genève</a> (FER Genève) and the Fédération des métiers du bâtiment (FMB).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many people also work in the numerous offices of <a href="/wiki/International_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International organisation">international organisations</a> located in Geneva (about 22,233 in March 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">Geneva Motor Show</a> is one of the most important international auto shows. It is held at <a href="/wiki/Palexpo" title="Palexpo">Palexpo</a>, a large convention centre next to the International Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009, Geneva was ranked as the fourth <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">most expensive city</a> in the world. Geneva moved up four places from eighth place the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-mercer.com_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mercer.com-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of &nbsp;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Geneva had an unemployment rate of 6.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were five<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="5 seems inherently improbable (July 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> people employed in the <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">primary economic sector</a> and about three<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="3 seems inherently improbable (July 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> businesses involved in this sector. 9,783 people were employed in the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">secondary sector</a> and there were 1,200 businesses in this sector. 134,429 people were employed in the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector</a>, with 12,489 businesses in this sector.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> There were 91,880 residents of the municipality who were employed in some capacity, with women making up 47.7% of the workforce. </p>
      <p>In 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the total number of <a href="/wiki/Full-time_equivalent" title="Full-time equivalent">full-time equivalent</a> jobs was 124,185. The number of jobs in the primary sector was four, all of which were in agriculture. The number of jobs in the secondary sector was 9,363 of which 4,863 or (51.9%) were in manufacturing and 4,451 (47.5%) were in construction. The number of jobs in the tertiary sector was 114,818. In the tertiary sector; 16,573 or 14.4% were in wholesale or retail sales or the repair of motor vehicles, 3,474 or 3.0% were in the movement and storage of goods, 9,484 or 8.3% were in a hotel or restaurant, 4,544 or 4.0% were in the information industry, 20,982 or 18.3% were the insurance or financial industry, 12,177 or 10.6% were technical professionals or scientists, 10,007 or 8.7% were in education and 15,029 or 13.1% were in health care.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 95,190 workers who commuted into the municipality and 25,920 workers who commuted away. The municipality is a net importer of workers, with about 3.7 workers entering the municipality for every one leaving. About 13.8% of the workforce coming into Geneva are coming from outside Switzerland, while 0.4% of the locals commute out of Switzerland for work.<sup id="cite_ref-commuter_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commuter-77">[75]</a></sup> Of the working population, 38.2% used public transportation to get to work, and 30.6% used a private car.<sup id="cite_ref-SFSO_44-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-44">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> is the most popular sport in Geneva.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Geneva is home to <a href="/wiki/Gen%C3%A8ve-Servette_HC" title="Genève-Servette HC">Genève-Servette HC</a>, which plays in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_(ice_hockey)" title="National League (ice hockey)">National League</a>. They play their home games in the 7,135-seat <a href="/wiki/Patinoire_des_Vernets" title="Patinoire des Vernets">Patinoire des Vernets</a>. In 2008 and 2010 the team made it to the league finals but lost to the <a href="/wiki/ZSC_Lions" title="ZSC Lions">ZSC Lions</a> and <a href="/wiki/SC_Bern" title="SC Bern">SC Bern</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> The team is by far the most popular one in both the city and the canton of Geneva, drawing three times more spectators than the <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The town is home to <a href="/wiki/Servette_FC" title="Servette FC">Servette FC</a>, a football club founded in 1890 and named after a borough on the right bank of the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a>. The home of Servette FC is the 30,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Stade de Genève">Stade de Genève</a>. Servette FC plays in the <a href="/wiki/Raiffeisen_Super_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Raiffeisen Super League">Raiffeisen Super League</a>. </p>
      <p>Geneva is home to the basketball team <a href="/wiki/Lions_de_Gen%C3%A8ve" title="Lions de Genève">Lions de Genève</a>, 2013 and 2015 champions of the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Basketball_League" title="Swiss Basketball League">Swiss Basketball League</a>. The team plays its home games in the <i>Pavilion des Sports</i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: 
       <a href="/wiki/Transports_Publics_Genevois" class="mw-redirect" title="Transports Publics Genevois">Transports Publics Genevois</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg/170px-Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg/255px-Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg/340px-Gare_de_Geneve_2236_Michelides.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a>

      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TCMC_(Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG/220px-TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG/330px-TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG/440px-TCMC_%28Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3036"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TCMC_(Tramway_Cornavin_-_Meyrin_-_CERN).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>TCMC (Tramway Cornavin – Meyrin – CERN)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The city is served by the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Cointrin_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva Cointrin International Airport">Geneva Cointrin International Airport</a>. It is connected by <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Airport_railway_station" title="Geneva Airport railway station">Geneva Airport railway station</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Gare de Genève-Aéroport</i>) to both the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Railways" title="Swiss Federal Railways">Swiss Federal Railways</a> network and the French <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> network, including links to Paris, Lyon, <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montpellier" title="Montpellier">Montpellier</a> by <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>. Geneva is connected to the motorway systems of both Switzerland (<a href="/wiki/A1_(Switzerland)" class="mw-redirect" title="A1 (Switzerland)">A1 motorway</a>) and France. </p>
      <p>Public transport by bus, trolleybus or tram is provided by <i><a href="/wiki/Transports_Publics_Genevois" class="mw-redirect" title="Transports Publics Genevois">Transports Publics Genevois</a></i>. In addition to an extensive coverage of the city centre, the network extends to most of the municipalities of the Canton, with a few lines reaching into France. Public transport by boat is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Mouettes_Genevoises" class="mw-redirect" title="Mouettes Genevoises">Mouettes Genevoises</a>, which link the two banks of the lake within the city, and by the <i><a href="/wiki/Compagnie_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale_de_Navigation_sur_le_lac_L%C3%A9man" title="Compagnie Générale de Navigation sur le lac Léman">Compagnie Générale de Navigation sur le lac Léman</a></i> which serves more distant destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Nyon" title="Nyon">Nyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yvoire" title="Yvoire">Yvoire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thonon-les-Bains" title="Thonon-les-Bains">Thonon</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vian-les-Bains" title="Évian-les-Bains">Évian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a> using both modern diesel vessels and vintage <a href="/wiki/Paddle_steamers" class="mw-redirect" title="Paddle steamers">paddle steamers</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG/200px-Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG/300px-Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG/400px-Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Train_Station_Geneva_2006_808.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Geneva Sécheron railway station
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Trains operated by <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Railways" title="Swiss Federal Railways">Swiss Federal Railways</a> connect the airport to the main station of <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Cornavin" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de Cornavin">Cornavin</a> in six minutes. Regional train services are being developed towards Coppet and Bellegarde. At the city limits two new railway stations have been opened since 2002: Genève-Sécheron (close to the UN and the <a href="/wiki/Conservatory_and_Botanical_Garden_of_the_City_of_Geneva" title="Conservatory and Botanical Garden of the City of Geneva">Botanical Gardens</a>) and Lancy-Pont-Rouge. </p>
      <p>In 2011 work started on the <a href="/wiki/CEVA_rail" title="CEVA rail">CEVA rail</a> (Cornavin – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eaux-Vives&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eaux-Vives (page does not exist)">Eaux-Vives</a> – Annemasse) project, first planned in 1884, which will connect Cornavin with the Cantonal hospital, Eaux-Vives railway station and <a href="/wiki/Annemasse" title="Annemasse">Annemasse</a>, in France. The link between the main railway station and the <a href="/wiki/Classification_yard" title="Classification yard">classification yard</a> of La Praille already exists; from there, the line will go mostly underground to the Hospital and Eaux-Vives, where it will link to the existing line to France. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg/200px-TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg/300px-TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg/400px-TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TOSA_Bus_at_PALEXPO_with_flag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>TOSA Bus at PALEXPO Flash bus stops
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In May 2013, the demonstrator <a href="/wiki/TOSA_Flash_Mobility,_Clean_City,_Smart_Bus" class="mw-redirect" title="TOSA Flash Mobility, Clean City, Smart Bus">electric bus system</a><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> with a capacity of 133 passengers commenced between <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Airport" title="Geneva Airport">Geneva Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palexpo" title="Palexpo">Palexpo</a>. The project aims to introduce a new system of mass transport with electric "flash" recharging of the buses at selected stops while passengers are disembarking and embarking.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Taxis in Geneva can be difficult to find, and may need to be booked in advance, especially in the early morning or at peak hours. Taxis can refuse to take babies and children because of <a href="/wiki/Infant_car_seat" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant car seat">seating</a> legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An ambitious project to close 200 streets in the centre of Geneva to cars was approved by the Geneva cantonal authorities in 2010 and was planned to be implemented over a span of four years (2010–2014), though as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, work on the project has yet to be started.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Water, natural gas and electricity are provided to the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_the_Canton_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of the Canton of Geneva">municipalities of the Canton of Geneva</a> by the state-owned <a href="/w/index.php?title=Services_Industriels_de_Gen%C3%A8ve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Services Industriels de Genève (page does not exist)">Services Industriels de Genève</a>, known as SIG. Most of the drinking water (80%) is extracted from the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">lake</a>; the remaining 20% is provided by <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">groundwater</a>, originally formed by infiltration from the Arve. 30% of the Canton's electricity needs is locally produced, mainly by three <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric</a> dams on the <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B4ne" title="Rhône">Rhône</a> (Seujet, Verbois and Chancy-Pougny). In addition, 13% of the electricity produced in the Canton is from the burning of waste at the <a href="/wiki/Waste_management#Incineration" title="Waste management">waste incineration facility</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Les_Cheneviers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Les Cheneviers (page does not exist)">Les Cheneviers</a>. The remaining needs (57%) are covered by imports from other cantons in Switzerland or other European countries; SIG buys only electricity produced by <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable methods</a>, and in particular does not use electricity produced using <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>. Natural gas is available in the City of Geneva, as well as in about two-thirds of the municipalities of the canton, and is imported from Western Europe by the Swiss company Gaznat. SIG also provides telecommunication facilities to carriers, <a href="/wiki/Service_provider" title="Service provider">service providers</a> and large enterprises. From 2003 to 2005, "Voisin, voisine" a <a href="/wiki/FTTH" class="mw-redirect" title="FTTH">fibre to the Home</a> pilot project with a <a href="/wiki/Triple_play_(telecommunications)" title="Triple play (telecommunications)">triple play</a> offering was launched to test the <a href="/wiki/End-user" class="mw-redirect" title="End-user">end-user</a> market in the Charmilles district. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_organisations">International organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: International organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: 
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_international_organizations_based_in_Geneva" title="List of international organizations based in Geneva">List of international organizations based in Geneva</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:WIPO3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/WIPO3.JPG/170px-WIPO3.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/WIPO3.JPG/255px-WIPO3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/WIPO3.JPG/340px-WIPO3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:WIPO3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 
         <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">World Intellectual Property Organization</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg/220px-ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg/330px-ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg/440px-ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ONU_Geneva_mainroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The assembly hall of the 
         <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations,_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Nations, Geneva">Palace of Nations</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Geneva is the European headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">United Nations</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations,_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Nations, Geneva">Palace of Nations</a> building, which was also the headquarters of the former League of Nations. Several agencies are headquartered at Geneva, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, the UN <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_High_Commissioner_for_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights">Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> , <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="International Baccalaureate Organization">International Baccalaureate Organization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">World Intellectual Property Organization</a>. </p>
      <p>Apart from the UN agencies, Geneva hosts many <a href="/wiki/Inter-governmental_organizations" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter-governmental organizations">inter-governmental organizations</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Maison_de_la_Paix" class="mw-redirect" title="Maison de la Paix">Maison de la Paix</a> building hosts the three Geneva centres supported by the Swiss Confederation: the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_International_Centre_for_Humanitarian_Demining" title="Geneva International Centre for Humanitarian Demining">International Centre for Humanitarian Demining</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Centre_for_the_Democratic_Control_of_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva Centre for the Democratic Control of Armed Forces">Centre for the Democratic Control of Armed Forces</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Centre_for_Security_Policy" title="Geneva Centre for Security Policy">Geneva Centre for Security Policy</a>, as well as other organisations active in the field of peace, international affairs and sustainable development.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Organizations on the European level include the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a> (EBU) and <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> (the European Organization for Nuclear Research) which is the world's largest particle physics laboratory. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Environment_Network" title="Geneva Environment Network">Geneva Environment Network</a> (GEN) publishes the Geneva Green Guide,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> an extensive listing of Geneva-based global organisations working on environment protection and sustainable development. A website,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> jointly run by the Swiss Government, the <a href="/wiki/World_Business_Council_for_Sustainable_Development" title="World Business Council for Sustainable Development">World Business Council for Sustainable Development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a>, includes accounts of how <a href="/wiki/NGO" class="mw-redirect" title="NGO">NGOs</a>, business, government and the UN cooperate. By doing so, it attempts to explain why Geneva has been picked by so many NGOs and UN bodies as their headquarters' location. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Organization_of_the_Scout_Movement" title="World Organization of the Scout Movement">World Organization of the Scout Movement</a> and the World Scout Bureau Central Office are headquartered in Geneva. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geneva&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Carro" title="Jean de Carro">Jean de Carro</a> (1770–1857) Vienna-based physician, promoted vaccination against smallpox <sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Casaubon" title="Isaac Casaubon">Isaac Casaubon</a> (1559–1614) a classical scholar and philologist <sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Meric_Casaubon" class="mw-redirect" title="Meric Casaubon">Meric Casaubon</a> (1599–1671) son of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Casaubon" title="Isaac Casaubon">Isaac Casaubon</a>, a French-English classical scholar <sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Challet-Venel" title="Jean-Jacques Challet-Venel">Jean-Jacques Challet-Venel</a> (1811–1893) politician, on the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Swiss Federal Council</a> 1864–1872</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Edward_Chalon" title="Alfred Edward Chalon">Alfred Edward Chalon</a> RA (1780–1860) portrait painter <sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/John_James_Chalon" title="John James Chalon">John James Chalon</a> RA (1778–1854) painter of landscapes, marine scenes and animal life <sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Henri_Christin%C3%A9" title="Henri Christiné">Henri Christiné</a> (1867–1941) French composer of sparkling, witty, jazzy musical plays<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Victor_Cherbuliez" title="Victor Cherbuliez">Victor Cherbuliez</a> (1829–1899) novelist and author <sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Clavi%C3%A8re" title="Étienne Clavière">Étienne Clavière</a> (1735–1793), banker and politician of the French revolution <sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Paulo_Coelho" title="Paulo Coelho">Paulo Coelho</a> (born 1947) Brazilian lyricist and novelist, author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Alchemist_(novel)" title="The Alchemist (novel)">The Alchemist</a></i>, residing in Geneva<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Colliard" title="Renée Colliard">Renée Colliard</a> (born 1933) former alpine skier, gold medallist at the <a href="/wiki/1956_Winter_Olympics" title="1956 Winter Olympics">1956 Winter Olympics</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Cramer" title="Gabriel Cramer">Gabriel Cramer</a> (1704–1752) Genevan mathematician <sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup></li>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Jurine" title="Louis Jurine">Louis Jurine</a> (1751–1819) physician, surgeon, naturalist and entomologist</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Krausz" title="Michael Krausz">Michael Krausz</a> (born 1942) American philosopher, an artist and orchestral conductor</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Adrien_Lachenal" title="Adrien Lachenal">Adrien Lachenal</a> (1849–1918), politician, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Council_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Council of Switzerland">Federal Council of Switzerland</a> 1892–1899</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Lachenal" title="François Lachenal">François Lachenal</a> (1918–1997) a publisher and diplomat</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Lachenal" title="Paul Lachenal">Paul Lachenal</a> (1884–1955), politician, co-founded <a href="/wiki/Orchestre_de_la_Suisse_Romande" title="Orchestre de la Suisse Romande">Orchestre de la Suisse Romande</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Marie_Lafor%C3%AAt" title="Marie Laforêt">Marie Laforêt</a> (born 1939) a French singer and actress <sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Lahbati" title="Sarah Lahbati">Sarah Lahbati</a> (born 1993), actress and singer <sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Franz_Lefort" title="Franz Lefort">François Le Fort</a> (1656–1699), first Russian Admiral<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Georges-Louis_Le_Sage" title="Georges-Louis Le Sage">Georges-Louis Le Sage</a> (1724–1803) a Genevan physicist, <a href="/wiki/Le_Sage%27s_theory_of_gravitation" title="Le Sage's theory of gravitation">Le Sage's theory of gravitation</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Leclerc_(theologian)" title="Jean Leclerc (theologian)">Jean Leclerc</a> (1657–1736) theologian and biblical scholar, promoted <a href="/wiki/Exegesis" title="Exegesis">exegesis</a> <sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Henri_Leconte" title="Henri Leconte">Henri Leconte</a> (born 1963) former French professional tennis player, men's singles finalist, French Open 1988</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> (1870–1924) lived in Geneva 1902–1905 as an exile from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean-%C3%89tienne_Liotard" title="Jean-Étienne Liotard">Jean-Étienne Liotard</a> (1702–1789) painter portraits in pastel,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> art connoisseur and dealer <sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Corinne_Maier" title="Corinne Maier">Corinne Maier</a> (born 1963) psychoanalyst, economist, and best-selling writer <sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ella_Maillart" title="Ella Maillart">Ella Maillart</a> (1903–1997) adventurer, travel writer and photographer, as well as a sportswoman</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Caesar_Malan" title="Solomon Caesar Malan">Solomon Caesar Malan</a> (1812–1894) oriental linguist and biblical scholar <sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Mallet_du_Pan" title="Jacques Mallet du Pan">Jacques Mallet du Pan</a> (1749–1800) Genevan-French royalist journalist <sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Marcet" title="Alexander Marcet">Alexander Marcet</a> FRS (1770–1822) physician who became a British citizen in 1800 <sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jane_Marcet" title="Jane Marcet">Jane Marcet</a> (1769–1858) an innovative writer of popular introductory science books <sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Martin_(composer)" title="Frank Martin (composer)">Frank Martin</a> (1890–1974), composer, editor of <a href="/wiki/The_Statesman%27s_Year_Book" class="mw-redirect" title="The Statesman's Year Book">The Statesman's Year Book</a></li> 
       <li>Dr. <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9odore_Maunoir" title="Théodore Maunoir">Théodore Maunoir</a> (1806–1869) co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9lie_Mauresmo" title="Amélie Mauresmo">Amélie Mauresmo</a> (born 1979) former professional tennis player and former world No.1</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9lemy_Menn" title="Barthélemy Menn">Barthélemy Menn</a> (1815–1893) a landscape painter, introduced painting <a href="/wiki/En_plein_air" title="En plein air">en plein air</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Menu_von_Minutoli" title="Heinrich Menu von Minutoli">Heinrich Menu von Minutoli</a> (1772–1846) a Prussian Generalmajor, explorer and archaeologist</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jacques-Barth%C3%A9lemy_Micheli_du_Crest" title="Jacques-Barthélemy Micheli du Crest">Jacques-Barthélemy Micheli du Crest</a> (1690–1766) military engineer, physicist and cartographer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Morgenstern" title="Stephanie Morgenstern">Stephanie Morgenstern</a> (born 1965) Canadian actress, filmmaker and screenwriter <sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Thierry_Moutinho" title="Thierry Moutinho">Thierry Moutinho</a> (born 1991), Swiss-Portuguese footballer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gustave_Moynier" title="Gustave Moynier">Gustave Moynier</a> (1826–1910), lawyer and co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a></li>
      </ul>

      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Necker" title="Jacques Necker">Jacques Necker</a> (1732–1804), banker and finance minister for <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI of France</a> <sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Albert_Necker" title="Louis Albert Necker">Louis Albert Necker</a> (1786–1861) a crystallographer and geographer, devised the <a href="/wiki/Necker_cube" title="Necker cube">Necker cube</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Felix_Neff" title="Felix Neff">Felix Neff</a> (1798–1829) Protestant divine and philanthropist <sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Newton" title="Alfred Newton">Alfred Newton</a> FRS HFRSE (1829–1907) English zoologist and ornithologist <sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Julie_Ordon" title="Julie Ordon">Julie Ordon</a> (born 1984), model and actress <sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup></li>

       <li>Faule Petitot (1572–1629), sculptor, cabinetmaker and architect, citizen of Geneva since 1615 <sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Petitot" title="Jean Petitot">Jean Petitot</a> (1607–1691) enamel painter, son of Faule <sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Piaget" title="Jean Piaget">Jean Piaget</a> (1896–1980) clinical psychologist, devised <a href="/wiki/Genetic_epistemology" title="Genetic epistemology">genetic epistemology</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Pinget" title="Robert Pinget">Robert Pinget</a> (1919–1997) an avant-garde French <a href="/wiki/Modernist" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist">modernist</a> <a href="/wiki/Nouveau_roman" title="Nouveau roman">nouveau roman</a> writer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/George_Pitt,_1st_Baron_Rivers" title="George Pitt, 1st Baron Rivers">George Pitt, 1st Baron Rivers</a> (1721–1803) English diplomat and politician <sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Polla" title="Barbara Polla">Barbara Polla</a> (born 1950), medical doctor, gallery owner, art curator and writer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/James_Pradier" title="James Pradier">James Pradier</a> (1790–1852), <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Geneva">Genevan</a> and then Swiss sculptor,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_sculpture" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoclassical sculpture">neoclassical</a> style</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Louis_Pr%C3%A9vost" title="Jean-Louis Prévost">Jean-Louis Prévost</a> (1838–1927) neurologist and physiologist</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Pr%C3%A9vost" title="Pierre Prévost">Pierre Prévost</a> (1751–1839) philosopher, physicist wrote the law of exchange in radiation <sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tariq_Ramadan" title="Tariq Ramadan">Tariq Ramadan</a> (born 1962) a Swiss Muslim academic, philosopher and writer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Marcel_Raymond" title="Marcel Raymond">Marcel Raymond</a> (1897–1981) a literary critic of French literature of the "<a href="/wiki/Geneva_School" title="Geneva School">Geneva School</a>"</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Flore_Revalles" title="Flore Revalles">Flore Revalles</a> (1889–1966), singer, dancer and actress <sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Pierre_Henri_Rieu" title="Charles Pierre Henri Rieu">Charles Pierre Henri Rieu</a> (1820–1902) Orientalist and Professor of Arabic <sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Prof <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Arthur_de_la_Rive" title="Auguste Arthur de la Rive">Auguste Arthur de la Rive</a> (1801–1873) a physicist, worked on the heat of gases <sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Charles-Gaspard_de_la_Rive" title="Charles-Gaspard de la Rive">Charles-Gaspard de la Rive</a> (1770–1834), physicist, psychiatrist and politician</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Jules_Pictet_de_la_Rive" title="François Jules Pictet de la Rive">François Jules Pictet de la Rive</a> (1809–1872) zoologist and palaeontologist <sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Marc_Rosset" title="Marc Rosset">Marc Rosset</a> (born 1970) former pro tennis player, gold medallist at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Olympic Games</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a> (1712–1778), writer and philosopher <sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Rousset" title="Jean Rousset">Jean Rousset</a> (1910–2002), literary critic and early <a href="/wiki/Structuralism" title="Structuralism">structuralism</a> writer of the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_School" title="Geneva School">Geneva School</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Xavier_Ruiz" title="Xavier Ruiz">Xavier Ruiz</a> (born 1970), film producer and director <sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup></li>
      </ul>

      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_de_Saussure" title="Ferdinand de Saussure">Ferdinand de Saussure</a> (1857–1913) a linguist and <a href="/wiki/Semiotician" class="mw-redirect" title="Semiotician">semiotician</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Horace_B%C3%A9n%C3%A9dict_de_Saussure" title="Horace Bénédict de Saussure">Horace Bénédict de Saussure</a> (1740–1799) geologist, meteorologist, physicist, and Alpine explorer <sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Nicolas-Th%C3%A9odore_de_Saussure" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolas-Théodore de Saussure">Nicolas-Théodore de Saussure</a> (1767–1845) chemist, studied plant physiology, advanced phytochemistry <sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Savary" title="Léon Savary">Léon Savary</a> (1895–1968), writer and journalist</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Schade" title="Michael Schade">Michael Schade</a> (born 1965) a Canadian operatic tenor <sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Jacob_Schweppe" title="Johann Jacob Schweppe">Johann Jacob Schweppe</a> (1740–1821) watchmaker developed <a href="/wiki/Schweppes" title="Schweppes">Schweppes</a> bottled <a href="/wiki/Carbonated_water" title="Carbonated water">carbonated water</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Marguerite_Sechehaye" title="Marguerite Sechehaye">Marguerite Sechehaye</a> (1887–1965) a psychotherapist, treated people with <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Segond" title="Louis Segond">Louis Segond</a> (1810–1885), theologian and translator, pastor in <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%AAne-Bougeries" title="Chêne-Bougeries">Chêne-Bougeries</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Philippe_Senderos" title="Philippe Senderos">Philippe Senderos</a> (born 1985), footballer, over 200 club caps and 57 for <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Senebier" title="Jean Senebier">Jean Senebier</a> (1742–1809) pastor and voluminous writer on vegetable physiology <sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Eugene_du_Simitiere" title="Pierre Eugene du Simitiere">Pierre Eugene du Simitiere</a> (1737–1784) naturalist, American patriot and portrait painter.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Michel_Simon" title="Michel Simon">Michel Simon</a> (1895–1975), actor <sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Charles_L%C3%A9onard_de_Sismondi" title="Jean Charles Léonard de Sismondi">Jean Charles Léonard de Sismondi</a> (1773–1842) historian and political economist <sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> (born 1983), lived in Geneva between 2007 and 2009, while working for the <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Soubeyran" title="Pierre Soubeyran">Pierre Soubeyran</a> (1706–1775) engraver, etcher and <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A9diste" class="mw-redirect" title="Encyclopédiste">Encyclopédiste</a> <sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Terry_Southern" title="Terry Southern">Terry Southern</a> (1924–1995) American author, essayist and screenwriter; lived in Geneva 1956–59 <sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ezekiel_Spanheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Ezekiel Spanheim">Ezekiel Spanheim</a> (1629–1710) Prussian diplomat</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Spanheim" title="Friedrich Spanheim">Friedrich Spanheim</a> (1632–1701) a Calvinistic theology professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leiden" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Leiden">University of Leiden</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Charles_Fran%C3%A7ois_Sturm" title="Jacques Charles François Sturm">Jacques Charles François Sturm</a> (1803–1855) French mathematician <sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Emile_Tadd%C3%A9oli" class="mw-redirect" title="Emile Taddéoli">Emile Taddéoli</a> (1879–1920), Swiss aviation pioneer</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Alain_Tanner" title="Alain Tanner">Alain Tanner</a> (born 1929), film director <sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Sigismund_Thalberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Sigismund Thalberg">Sigismund Thalberg</a> (1812–1871), Austrian composer and pianist <sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Max_Thurian" title="Max Thurian">Max Thurian</a> (1921–1996), theologian, known as Frère Max</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Tirard" title="Pierre Tirard">Pierre Tirard</a> (1827–1893) French politician <sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Rodolphe_T%C3%B6pffer" title="Rodolphe Töpffer">Rodolphe Töpffer</a> (1799–1846) teacher, author, painter, cartoonist and caricaturist <sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wolfgang-Adam_T%C3%B6pffer" title="Wolfgang-Adam Töpffer">Wolfgang-Adam Töpffer</a> (1766–1847) painter of landscapes and watercolors <sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Vico_Torriani" title="Vico Torriani">Vico Torriani</a> (1920–1998), singer, actor, show host <sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Georges_Trombert" title="Georges Trombert">Georges Trombert</a> (1874–1949) a French fencer, silver and bronze medallist at the <a href="/wiki/1920_Summer_Olympics" title="1920 Summer Olympics">1920 Summer Olympics</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9odore_Tronchin" title="Théodore Tronchin">Théodore Tronchin</a> (1709–1781) a Genevan physician <sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Turrettini" title="François Turrettini">François Turrettini</a> (1623–1687) a Genevan-Italian Reformed scholastic theologian <sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Alphonse_Turrettini" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Alphonse Turrettini">Jean Alphonse Turrettini</a> (1671–1737), reformed theologian <sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Vivares" title="François Vivares">François Vivares</a> (1709–1780) French landscape-engraver, active in England <sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Johann_Vogel" title="Johann Vogel">Johann Vogel</a> (born 1977) former footballer, played 94 games for <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a></li> 
       <li>Prince <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Volkonsky" title="Andrei Volkonsky">Andrei Volkonsky</a> (1933–2008) Russian composer of classical music and harpsichordist <sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> (1694–1778) French philosopher, historian, dramatist and man of letters; lived at <a href="/wiki/Les_D%C3%A9lices" title="Les Délices">Les Délices</a> 1755–1760 <sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/R._Norris_Williams" title="R. Norris Williams">R. Norris Williams</a> (1891–1968) American tennis player and <a href="/wiki/RMS_Titanic" title="RMS Titanic">RMS Titanic</a> survivor</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Wissmer" title="Pierre Wissmer">Pierre Wissmer</a> (1915–1992), Swiss-French composer, pianist and music teacher</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jean_Ziegler" title="Jean Ziegler">Jean Ziegler</a> (born 1934), politician and sociologist</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Reto_Ziegler" title="Reto Ziegler">Reto Ziegler</a> (born 1986) footballer, has played 35 games for <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a></li>
      </ul>
